Free Talk

Starting from the Twenty-Four Histories 229

— Ling Mo

It seems that Liang Qichao once said that the Twenty-Four Histories are essential reading for Chinese scholars – whether they study engineering or agriculture. However, he also believed it was a last resort. He lamented that China did not yet have specialized histories or comprehensive histories, so people still had to rely on these private records of emperors, books of mutual destruction, and generally, piles of antiques. In his writings, he aspired to create a decent comprehensive history himself, but unfortunately, most of his energy was spent on being an official and playing cards. Whether his disciples accepted his remaining ambition is unknown, but it has been more than ten years since his promise, and those continuing his wish seem to be nowhere in sight. The fact that China still lacks a proper comprehensive history is why the Twenty-Four Histories remain important historical materials, and why they continue to circulate.

The enlightened nine-volume set of the Twenty-Five Histories is now available for pre-order. This approach is commendable in several ways. Compiling this massive work into just nine volumes makes people feel that it is not an unreadable book, subtly increasing their courage to read it. However, being able to read it is one thing, but what to do after reading the entire set is another. Horizontally, those who specialize in studying various aspects of a particular dynasty only need the historical books of that dynasty and the two dynasties before and after it. Therefore, for the convenience of these readers, the Twenty-Four Histories should not be sold as a complete set at all. Those who specialize in studying a particular aspect of each dynasty need only a portion of each history. For their convenience, the publication method should be changed. The former is not a significant problem, but the latter is worth noting.

The Astronomical Research Institute bought the complete Bai Na edition of the Twenty-Four Histories to study the astronomical records of past dynasties. However, they can only use the treatises on astronomy, treatises on the Five Elements, etc. The treatises on astronomy and the treatises on the Five Elements are truly unreadable or unnecessary for ordinary readers. Although it is not easy for us to newly compile a collection of astronomical history data, it is not difficult to compile and print all the treatises on astronomy and the treatises on the Five Elements from the Twenty-Four Histories. With a little more effort, taking the main contents from the Book of Han, the Book of Sui, and the History of Ming, noting the same text and different text from the other histories, and adopting the records of encyclopedias like the General Records, it would not be difficult to create a more usable book. Otherwise, reprinting them as they are would also be more convenient to use. It is generally accepted that the Twenty-Four Histories can only serve as reference books, and reference books should have the advantages of reference books.

This reminds me of the Complete Collection of Illustrations of Books. Chinese encyclopedias are mostly classified. Since they are classified, they can be published separately. Because the fourteenth edition of the Encyclopedia Britannica has become so large that it is not needed for general use, in addition to the complete set, separate classified volumes are compiled and sold separately. We, on the other hand, have encyclopedias that are originally classified but must be sold as a complete set. The difference between progress and conservatism is truly too great. In fact, if the editions of the treatises on astronomy in the Twenty-Four Histories could be printed, then the sections on astronomy and calendrical methods in the Complete Collection of Illustrations of Books could be abandoned.

When reprinting the Twenty-Four Histories, at least the treatises and tables of each history should be compiled and printed separately (but genealogical records like the Zhao family genealogy in the History of Song should be deleted decisively, and only a catalog retained). The imperial chronicles and biographies could be arranged according to surnames, and a large dictionary of personal names could be compiled, with the original order of the books listed as an appendix. The foreign accounts – accounts of the Four Barbarians, the Xiongnu, the Western Regions – could also be compiled into separate volumes. Modern Western scholars of China have compiled all the materials on the Xiongnu, Turks, etc., from the Twenty-Four Histories into specialized books, and Chinese publishers are translating them back and selling them as new works. From the perspective of book merchants seeking profit, this is of course understandable, but from an academic perspective, it cannot but be considered a disgrace. If our reprint publishers of the Twenty-Four Histories were willing to compile them by country and include related texts, their achievements would be more than just a publishing revolution, but immortal achievements.

The redundancy in the Old and New Books of Tang and the Old and New Histories of Yuan would naturally disappear if the above method were followed. In fact, even without dismantling and recompiling the Twenty-Four Histories, it would be better to combine these two histories within one book, rather than having two overlapping books. Using the new as the main text, and editing the material from the old book, deleting the same material and annotating the different material under the same material, they could coexist and be easier to review, and the reduction in length would be a bonus.

The classified and recompiled Twenty-Four Histories would not change the essence of the original books in the slightest. Everyone could still find what they were looking for, the only difference being that it would be easier to find. This is not dissecting the original books, but rather gathering what was originally dissected. This should be a perfect solution, but no one has mentioned it so far, probably because those with a superficial understanding are unwilling to go to the trouble, while those with lofty goals feel that this is just a scissors-and-paste job. But I believe that without this scissors-and-paste work, the specialized histories and comprehensive histories of those with lofty goals will become increasingly distant.

The pricing of the nine-volume set is also considered very cheap, and their lack of focus on high profits is also commendable. However, if we are only talking about low prices, the binding prices for popular novels that are currently being reprinted seem to be able to be more than halved. But even if you can buy the Twenty-Four Histories for ten or eight yuan, the part that you don't need to read is a waste of money, and it is an especially irreplaceable loss if you don't know what you don't need to read and waste your energy reading it. If we can never have a well-recompiled Twenty-Four Histories, then that's fine, but if we can have a day when it is compiled, then another identical reprint would also be a waste. This reprint is probably irreversible now, but if there are those who want to reprint it again, we hope that they will not only think about competing with lower prices, but that there is actually a better way out in terms of compilation and distribution.

On Size 230

— Jian Ge

If someone is arguing about the issue of essays and popular language, then I am willing to provide some discussion materials...

What is large?

Generally, long articles are large pieces… short articles are essays. But looking at the writings of important people today, which often run to hundreds of thousands of words, are these large pieces? If you think those words are "large," then the literary world will know how to exert itself from now on. Just keep writing, the longer the bigger, the bigger the longer, you can break the world's record for works.

From ancient times to the present, poems of more than 10,000 words are rarely seen; Yu Chuan Sheng seemed to be writing desperately, like Bian Yun Yue Shi, but it doesn't seem that long; the memorable sentences are very simple, but poetry has never been considered an essay. It can be seen that specializing in form cannot distinguish size.

There are very short articles in ancient times, such as Ban Mengjian's Lezheng Ranming, Lanting Xu, and Taohuayuan Ji. Are these essays? These all seem to be large pieces. It is also difficult to distinguish the size of the content, because what is written is so different.

Then let's talk about Yuan Zhonglang. This type of writing is an essay. The content is about how to drink tea, eat, play with flowers and plants, and travel the mountains and rivers. But understanding the art of living is not just Zhonglang, talking about elegance is not just Zhonglang, this type of writing is not just Zhonglang who can write, there are so many people in ancient times who understood the art of living, especially in the Six Dynasties. It can be seen that you cannot use the writer as a standard.

Form, content, and writer cannot be used as standards, it can be seen that large pieces and essays are vain calculations and unnecessary disputes. But in the end, works can be distinguished as great or not, and this distinction lies in the work itself and the personality from which it originates.

Therefore, while writing essays, one may also oppose or hate "essays." Just as you can still scold people for talking while talking yourself. Commentators say that it is inappropriate to attack essays with essays, then attackers should write hundreds of volumes to attack "essays." Then writing an essay should support "essays."

There must be a day, then writing essays will really become "small," and then speaking loudly that this is really great, then what will become of it.

Casual Literary Talk 231

— Hua Yu

(9) Specialization or Universalization?

Here, we encounter another big problem... Chinese language is very different in different places. With just a rough distinction, there are five kinds: Northern dialect, Jiangzhe dialect, Lianghu-Chuan-Gui dialect, Fujian dialect, and Cantonese. And within these five kinds, there are still small distinctions. Now, when using Latin letters to write, should we write in standard language or local dialect? If we write in standard language, people won't understand; if we write in local dialect, people in other places won't understand, and it will be isolated, not as good as the nationally-used Chinese characters. This is a big drawback!

My idea is... in the initial enlightenment period, each place should write in its own local dialect, without having to worry about not being understood by other places. Before the use of Latin writing, our illiterate people did not communicate with each other using Chinese characters, so there is no new harm added. On the contrary, there are new benefits, at least in the same language area, people can exchange opinions and absorb knowledge with each other -- of course, at the same time, someone has to write some useful books. The question is whether the popular language in each place should be specialized or universalized in the future?

In dialects and local languages, there are many profound words, which we call "refined words," and they are very meaningful to use, just like the use of classics in classical Chinese, and listeners also find it interesting... Each dialect, the grammar and vocabulary, should be further refined and developed, which is specialization. This is very beneficial to literature, it can make articles more interesting than articles using only general language. But specialization also has its dangers. I don't know about linguistics, but looking at biology, specialization often leads to extinction. Many animals and plants before humans became extinct because they were too specialized, lost their variability, and could not cope with changes in the environment, so they had to become extinct. Fortunately, we humans are not considered specialized animals, so please don't worry. The masses have literature, want literature, but should never be sacrificed for literature, otherwise, its absurdity and the living sages who want eight-tenths of the Chinese people to be illiterate to preserve Chinese characters are no different. Therefore, I think that dialects should be used in the enlightenment period, but at the same time, ordinary grammar and vocabulary should be gradually added. First use the inherent, is the popularization of a local language, adding the new, is the popularization of a national language.

The plans discussed by a few scholars in the study are of course mostly unworkable, but it is not a good idea to let everything take its course. Now, in the docks, public institutions, and universities, there is indeed something that looks like a standard language. Everyone speaks neither "Mandarin" nor Beijing dialect, and each carries a local accent and tone, but it is not a dialect. Even if it is difficult to speak and difficult to hear, it can always be said and understood. If it is sorted out and helped to develop, it is also a branch of popular language, and it may even be the main force in the future. I said that we need to add new things to the dialects - and the source of the new things is in this place. When this kind of thing comes out of nature and is artificially added - popularization, our popular language will be roughly unified.

Of course, we still have to do it after this. After a long time, the language becomes more consistent, and things that are as good as a 'refined word', and even more alive than the classics, gradually form, and literature becomes more brilliant. It can't be done right away. You think, the Chinese characters that national quintessence scholars regard as treasures, it didn't take three or four thousand years to create this pile of strange achievements?

As for the question of who should do it, that goes without saying... it is enlightened scholars. Some people say... "The affairs of the masses should be done by the masses themselves!" That is of course correct, but you have to see what role you are talking about. If you are talking about the masses, then there is one thing that is correct, that is, they have to do it themselves, and what is wrong is pushing away the helpers. If you are talking about scholars, then it is completely different; he is using beautiful words to control the text and protect his own honor.

Confucius 232

— Cao Juren

— Using materials from The Analects, The Hereditary House of Confucius, and The Biographies of the Disciples of Zhongni —

(1)

"Mom, where's my dad?"

"Child, you're still young; I'll tell you when you're older!"

"They all say I'm a bastard!"

"Don't pay attention to them, they're all ill-mannered!"

Yan hugged Zhongni in her arms, tears dripping one by one on her son's face.

"Mom, why are you crying?"

Yan wiped away her tears with her right sleeve, lowered her head and kissed Zhongni's forehead, and said in a low voice...

"Child, you're still young!"

This big mystery hid in Zhongni's heart, year after year, he wanted to become an adult quickly, and his mother would tell him the answer. Year after year, his mother never told him the answer after all. One day, Yan became seriously ill and called Zhongni to come to the bedside...

"Child, come here, I'll tell you..."

Before she could speak, Yan's voice was already choked up. Seeing his mother in such pain, Zhongni quickly comforted her...

"Mom, it's okay to tell me in detail when you feel better."

"Your mother's illness won't get better! Child, regarding your father's matter, the mother of Man Fu (that person from Zou), she knows everything clearly."

Soon, Yan died. At that time, Zhongni was already twenty-four years old. He learned a little about the process of his parents' union from Man Fu's mother, as well as the location of his father's burial after his death. He buried his father's coffin and his mother's coffin together on the side of Fang Mountain. After the earthen grave was finished, Zhongni lay on the grave, wailing sorrowfully...

"Mom, I know everything clearly!"

"Boyu! Have you memorized the Songs of Zhou and the Songs of Zhao?"

"Yes, I've memorized them long ago; what's the use of memorizing those mountain songs?"

"Child, human relationships and worldly wisdom, human relationships and worldly wisdom, this is all human relationships and worldly wisdom!"

"Dad, I'll recite it for you...

"Guan guan cry the ospreys,

On the islet in the river.

The modest, retiring, virtuous, young lady:

For our prince a good mate she is.

Here long, there short, is the duckweed;

To the left, to the right, they pluck it.

The modest, retiring, virtuous, young lady:

Waking and sleeping, he desired her.

He sought her and found her not;

Waking and sleeping, he thought about her.

Long he thought; oh! long and anxiously;

He turned and tossed about, never getting sleep."

Zhongni closed his eyes and listened quietly to Boyu's singing, tapping lightly on the table with his hand. Suddenly, he said as if he felt something...

"Boyu, you may leave!"

Boyu walked out of Zhongni's study, and Zhongni still heard his singing from afar...

"In the wild there lies a dead deer,

And it is wrapped up with white grass.

There was a young girl with thoughts of spring;

A good youth seduced her!

·················"

Zhongni said to himself in a low voice...

"Mom, I know everything clearly!"

Younger Brother (9) 233

— Zhou Wen

Later, our troops were defeated, and that relative also didn't resolve anything, life in the hometown was even more difficult, and the small store at home had to close down, so my younger brother and I had to think of other ways to go. My younger brother entered a military academy again, and so did I. At this time, everyone would only play together on weekends. Although that strange temper was not thrown away.

I remember when he graduated, I told him I would buy him a leather belt. That day, while he hadn't come yet, I asked several classmates to go buy it together. Because we didn't have much money, we bought a medium one. When we were waiting for him in the park, I was very happy to give it to him, thinking that he would also be very happy; but he took the belt and looked at it, then looked at the widest belt he had borrowed to tie around his waist, his face suddenly turned green, his eyes straightened, he threw the belt on the chair with a snap, and turned to leave. My friends were all surprised. It made me want to jump up and hit him a few times, but I finally calmed down, pulled him back, and promised to buy him another one. He then sat down angrily in the midst of many surprised glances.

From then on, he was assigned to another unit, and we had no chance to meet. And my life also began to change rapidly.

Grains

Futures Flour and Wheat Fall Again 246

||A Clear Trend Towards Decline||

Yesterday, the flour market saw extreme turbulence in all months after the morning opening. Although there was no quotation for foreign wheat, market sentiment showed a clear trend towards decline. Sales in North China were stagnant, and the routes to various towns and villages in the interior were blocked due to dried-up rivers, making it impossible to transport goods. As a result, the mooncake sales market, which usually occurs every year, was also cut off. Therefore, when pricing opened, the current month initially opened at 0.45, but later long positions were released, and prices gradually declined. In the distant months, non-industry long positions, seeing the unfavorable situation, also desperately sold off, with each month falling uniformly by 0.3 to 0.4 points compared to the previous day. By the afternoon opening, the market in each month had changed drastically again. Because factories were selling off accumulated spot goods, the high-value long positions were swept away like leaves in a storm and could no longer resist. Therefore, the opening price immediately fell again, and the intensity of the trend was beyond expectations. The current month fell to a low of 0.3825, a huge decline of about 0.5 yuan from the previous month's highest and lowest. This irrational situation, where prices rise without reason and fall without reflecting reality, is something that all operators should repeatedly reflect on. October to January also fell below 0.5 yuan. February fell to the 0.51 level. Although Guangdong and Shandong merchants were buying, the rest were less active. As a result, the current month fell by 0.0625, October fell by 0.07, November fell by 0.08, December fell by 0.0775, January fell by 0.07, and February fell by 0.065.

Yesterday, the wheat market showed an extremely soft trend in all months after the morning opening. Although there was no quotation for foreign wheat, because factories had fewer purchases due to the abundance of spot wheat, people both inside and outside the industry lost interest in this situation. Those with goods either sought to sell them or entered into a standard agreement. Therefore, after pricing opened, the prices in each month were weak, falling by 0.07 to 0.08 compared to the previous day's closing price. By the afternoon opening, the market had fallen even more sharply. Due to the intense decline in the flour market and the free selling of outside long positions, each month went downhill like a river, without looking back. According to industry insiders' speculation, it is feared that rural bankruptcies will make it impossible to expect good commodity prices, and a further heavy decline is also possible. As a result, the current month fell by 0.16, October fell by 0.17, November fell by 0.19, December fell by 0.18, January fell by 0.16, and February fell by 0.14. It was heard that the asking price for spot wheat was 3.7 yuan, but the factories were less interested. According to experts, prices must return to 0.6 before they can be moved.

Spring and Autumn

Little Western Heaven 256

— By Zhang Henshui

As he said this, he kept nodding. Cheng Zhiqian said, "I've eaten. People in Xi'an all eat two meals. They eat this afternoon meal at four o'clock. I ate at a friend's house." Zhang Jiefu interjected, "Things in Xi'an are really expensive, beer sells for one yuan and seventy or eighty cents a bottle." Cheng Zhiqian said, "Things from the East are always expensive here. People coming here should be prepared to endure hardship, these things from the East, it's better not to use them." Zhang Jiefu got the opportunity to talk to that person, and didn't seize the opportunity, but first asked for advice for a while. Then he interjected, "I just heard that Mr. Cheng is going to visit Zhouling. This is really a place we should visit first when we come to the Northwest. Is there a car to get there?" Cheng Zhiqian said, "I haven't inquired about that. I've decided to go." Li Shilian said, "Aren't you going by car?" Cheng Zhiqian said, "A friend who just came promised to lend me his car." Li Shilian said, "Mr. Cheng is very elegant, and must have a great interest in archeology. The culture of the Northwest has great value in history, and it is necessary to investigate it. We admire Mr. Cheng very much for coming here with the purpose of enduring hardship." Zhang Jiefu said, "Mr. Cheng, please come and sit in our room, okay? It's rare to meet in this place." Cheng Zhiqian felt that the two were very polite, so he had to follow Zhang Jiefu into his room. Zhang Jiefu invited him to sit down and immediately took out the biscuits in the basket to offer him. Li Shilian remembered that he had brought canned goods, and there was still a can of candied pears that he hadn't eaten, so he also asked the room attendant to open it and send it to Cheng Zhiqian to eat. After talking for a long time, Cheng Zhiqian proposed to visit Zhouling tomorrow. If the two of you are willing to go, you can go together. Li Shilian said, "We are very willing to go. But Director Wu is accompanying Mr. Cheng, so it might be a little inconvenient for us to go together, right?" Cheng Zhiqian laughed, "That's okay, I'll introduce you two in a moment." As soon as Zhang and Li heard this, they stood up at the same time and bowed to Cheng Zhiqian several times, repeatedly saying thank you, thank you. (12)

White Tea 257

— By Li Kui

People who have lived in Beiping, no one does not know the story of this white tea. This story, like that old host in Shaguoju who once served the Empress Dowager Cixi, is being passed down by the general public.

It is said that white tea is extremely precious, and can be said to be the head of tea. In the Qing Dynasty, only the royal family could afford to eat it, let alone the poor, they did not even have the eye-blessing of seeing white tea.

But now the remnants of the old dynasty living in Beiping (they wear old-fashioned gowns and robes, and walk swaying, as if going to see their masters. They are still dreaming of the past!) they have already become so poor that some sell their daughters to brothels to become prostitutes, and some live from meal to meal.

But they are still eating white tea｜this is called poor style. Because they used to eat white tea; now if they don't eat white tea, wouldn't it seem decadent! He is still unwilling to show his decadence. Although they have already fallen to the point where they can no longer fall.

They are so embarrassed that eating has become a problem, where do they have money to buy white tea to eat? To be honest, they can't afford to buy white tea, even better tea they can't afford! And they can't afford to eat it!

When guests come, because they don't have tea, they take out some of the old tea they have drunk before, pick out some leaves that are neat, and put them in the teacup; this not only has no taste at all, but also has no color at all!

But if the guests ask curiously, they will say very politely: "This is the best white tea!"

Although the guests do not believe their nonsense; but it is not good to say anything; they can only nod in agreement. Who would be willing to expose their pitiful secret!

Tidbits 258

On the track of life, I don't know how many happy things there are; I also don't know how many sad things there are. Sadness and happiness are the sunny and rainy days of the mind; they are two cyclically playing notes on the strings of life.

Women and money are often the main driving force for disrupting public order. So many tragedies in the world are all caused by them. (Zhen)

On Yuyuan Road 259

— By You Huansheng

Avenue Joffre in the French Concession is mysterious. Nanjing Road in the British Concession is noisy. But Yuyuan Road is not comparable to the mysterious Avenue Joffre, nor the noisy Nanjing Road. Tall buildings on both sides face each other, and the road in the middle stretches horizontally. Trolleybuses and buses come and go non-stop, private cars and taxis, pass in an instant, come over in an instant. There are not as many people as on Nanjing Road and Avenue Joffre, it is a quiet road.

Paramount Dance Hall stands proudly at the intersection of Yuyuan Road. Once the lights are on, the bright electric lights illuminate it like daytime. Young masters, modern ladies, business tycoons, and political bosses are intoxicated in it, laughing and dancing, but the intoxicating music cannot be heard outside, how quiet it is!

On Yuyuan Road, there are banks, bookstores, and various shops. There are also various different lanes, neighborhoods, and villages, which are very modern, with bathrooms, garages, water heaters, air conditioning, everything. In addition, the elegant private gardens with flowers, trees, and plants add a lot of color.

Huierkang Restaurant, Saint Anna Dance Hall, and all kinds of consumption and food halls are all together. The quiet and vast Zhaofeng Park is also at the end of Yuyuan Road, which is why the word "quiet" is added to Yuyuan Road.

Gold! On Yuyuan Road, in the city, in the world, everything can be bought, mysterious, noisy, and quiet roads are all colored by gold. Alas! Gold! Almighty gold!

Records of the Drifting Fragrance of the Imperial Incense 260

— Originally by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Here, we can imagine even more that the reason why their descendants do not come to sweep the tombs must be that their economic situation is really so distressed that they cannot bear it; and the distress that the dead feel underground is even more unbearable to imagine!

Those barren graves that she was pointing to are actually charitable cemeteries; charitable cemeteries are run by local charitable organizations, and not a good deed that individuals can undertake, which is where the old lady misunderstood.

Speaking of tomb sweeping, although everyone's original intention is the same; but its form, due to the different economic abilities of each person, must be divided into the following types: The first type is wealthy families. They must first prepare a very rich feast of wine and dishes, and have servants carry it, respectfully and reverently, to display it in front of their ancestral tombs; while burning paper ingots, they kowtow and salute. After displaying it for several tens of minutes, they take all the wine and dishes back, and send it all into their own stomachs. The second type is middle-class families. Although they are not so powerless as to prepare wine and dishes, their ancestors did not explicitly demand them, so they decided to simplify things; but paper ingots are always brought to be burned, because it has been a tradition since ancient times, although no one has ever presented any evidence, everyone deeply believes that after the paper ingots are burned, the dead can get real silver; fortunately, the living do not need paper ingots, as long as they spend a little money, they can buy a lot of paper ingots. If they really want them to burn the banknotes, money notes, and foreign money that the living need to use themselves to the dead, they would rather die than do it! The third type is families below the middle class, the economic situation of these families, probably described by the four words "robbing Peter to pay Paul" is certainly very accurate. (121)

Seeking Heaven Is Not as Good as Digging the Ground 261

— (Xia Hu)

Opening rivers to prevent drought, there are clear instructions in ancient times. In the twelfth year of Tongzhi in our Anhui, Mr. Zhang Mingzhai opened the Xincheng Changhe River, which had water until the thirty-fourth year of Guangxu, which shows the importance of opening rivers. Now the rivers are polluted and no one cares, if we don't take advantage of this drought year to open the rivers, are we going to ask the sixty-third generation Zhang Tianshi for rain forever? Some people say that the water and funds taken from the people in peacetime can always be used for the people now, right?

Friends who are shouting to go to the countryside, please practice what you say, go to the countryside to see the tragic situation of the countryside, it is better to act than to sit and talk, the personal visit of a certain county magistrate to the countryside, the farmers' automatic opening of ditches and digging ditches can be taken as an example, seeking heaven is not as good as digging the ground, this is the time.

Cold Talk 263

— (Yang Yusheng)

In Europe and America, it is said that "heat" runs faster than "cold," so everywhere in the folk is "hot air." At the same time, they are very disgusted with "cold," so the term "Catch Cold" is prevalent. In the minds of Europeans and Americans, "cold" is considered to "injure" the "customs" of the people!

Chinese folk is not like this, it seems that there is a "malaria ghost" at work. This malaria ghost probably died of old age in the summer, fearing heat and liking cold, so "heat" spreads very slowly, and cannot last long, it subsides in a flash of five minutes. But [cold] progresses very quickly. And can last for one or two years or even decades! Therefore, the Chinese folk is a piece of cold!

Visiting friends, Jian Wang Yujun, no news since January 28, where are you currently living? Please send a letter to the original address as expected. (Ju Ping)

Miscellaneous Talk

Talking About Travelogues 264

— Chen Shicheng

"To believe everything in books is worse than having no books." Opening my mouth to recite Mencius, I am not using Master Mencius to put on a show to scare people... In this day and age, Master Mencius's show no longer works. China is modernized; the psychology of modern people... whether it's people or academics, they've all been married off｜other people's wives are better｜. To scare people, it might be more effective to borrow foreign shows like Bernard Shaw and Gorky... I recite Mencius to... practice the eight-legged essay style of playing tricks, saying "To believe everything in travelogues is worse than having no travelogues." The common problem with travelogues is inaccuracy; because of their inaccuracy, they cannot be fully believed.

The authors who write travelogues do not intentionally want to be inaccurate. The reasons for their inaccuracy are roughly the following five: (1) deliberately seeking perfection, (2) abusing rhetoric, (3) differences in knowledge and environment, (4) differences in physical strength, (5) weakness in observation.

A desire to win is a common human psychology; when writing, if you can't come up with a unique way to win, you can't overwhelm the crowd. So the six words "unwilling to speak ordinary words" is a compliment in Chinese literature. Although travelogues should be a kind of factual writing; they can't avoid being influenced by this psychology.

Rhetoric is an indispensable and important condition in writing; describing scenery especially relies on its great power. Rhetoric in classical Chinese often becomes a kind of "idiom." In order to avoid the ridicule of "fabrication," they strive to apply "idioms"; so even stone walls that are dozens of feet high, and deep pools of several fathoms, are all described with the idioms "walls standing a thousand fathoms high" and "bottomless abyss of ten thousand fathoms." Eight feet is a fathom, a thousand fathoms is eight thousand feet, ten feet is a zhang, ten thousand zhang is one hundred thousand feet. Who has ever seen a stone wall eight thousand feet high, or a pool one hundred thousand feet deep? In fact, we can't say, and dare not say that there are no such high or deep walls and pools; but it won't always be that the stone wall is exactly eight thousand feet high, and the pool is exactly one hundred thousand feet deep, without any difference. Abusing rhetoric and idioms is the second reason for the inaccuracy of travelogues.

People's ideas change with environment and knowledge. People who grow up in cities, as long as they leave the noisy cities and go to the countryside; even if there is no beautiful scenery, they feel that it is quiet and pleasant, picturesque everywhere, making people feel refreshed and happy. Those who are used to living in the countryside will not have the above feelings. Also, people who have never seen mountains in their lives, once they have the opportunity to see the North and South Peaks by the West Lake in Hangzhou or the Tianping and Tianchi Mountains in Suzhou, will naturally feel their greatness and loftiness. If you change to someone who has climbed Tianmu and Xuetou, they will not have that feeling of loftiness and greatness. If you change to someone who has worshipped the Five Sacred Mountains and traveled to Mount Emei and Snow Mountain, not only the North and South Peaks and Tianping and Tianchi are just small hills; even the Xuetou Mountains are not considered very high. Since people's environment and knowledge are different, even if they are traveling to the same place, their feelings are also different. Then the travelogues they write will naturally not be consistent.

Physical strength is also different, like environment and knowledge. For those who are strong walkers, running a hundred or eighty miles is nothing! Those who can't run find it difficult to walk three or five miles. Those who are good at climbing mountains don't find it difficult to climb very high peaks; those who are not good at climbing mountains feel breathless and leg sore after walking a few steps on a mountain road! Affected by physical weakness, they can't help but make the near seem far, and the low seem high. I have seen a travelogue about Ge Ling in Hangzhou... the author started from Hangzhou and walked to the foot of Ge Ling, saying that his feet were already tired; when climbing the mountain, he was like the end of a crossbow, and it was difficult to walk. He also described Ge Ling as unreachably high. People who have never been to Hangzhou, after reading this record, will definitely wonder how far Ge Ling is from Hangzhou, and how high the mountain is? However, those who have traveled to Ge Ling can't help but smile silently. This is clear evidence that physical weakness causes the travelogue to be inaccurate.

When we travel, the mountains, rivers, plants, and trees we see, of course, need to be described when writing the record. How high is the mountain? How wide is the river? We can't measure them one by one with a ruler; we can only judge by our own observation. Although we can't be very accurate, we can't just say whatever we want; if our common sense is insufficient and our observation is weak; then the result of speculation will be too far from the truth; wouldn't that become a joke?

Shen Bao This Local Supplement

Talking

A Message to Friends Who Are "Slow at Heart" 265

— A Long

When discussing any kind of academic subject, or any kind of problem, whether the object of discussion is worth discussing or not, there must first be two attitudes: (1) an attitude of research, and (2) an attitude of humility.

Because of the former, "The wise man sometimes makes a mistake in a thousand thoughts, and the fool sometimes gains something in a thousand thoughts," therefore the more academic subjects are researched, the more refined they become, and the more thoroughly the problems are discussed. With the latter, "Fullness invites loss, and humility benefits," although these two words are also old sayings, they are still useful in the place of being a person or doing research. Assuming that an academic subject or a problem only has my own opinions, and absolutely does not allow the opinions of others, this narrow-minded view is still used by previous scholars to form parties and attack dissidents to obliterate everything, which is absolutely unacceptable.

After this magazine published Mr. He's article criticizing the Literature One-Year Anniversary Special Issue "Me and Literature" last month, in the Literature Forum of Literature Volume 3, No. 3, there was Mr. Hua's article "A Message to Friends Who Are Impatient at Heart," which naturally launched a big attack on Mr. He's article. Which of these two articles is right and which is wrong, I don't have much energy and time to criticize, but Mr. Hua has a few words in the article "A Message to Friends Who Are Impatient at Heart," and these few words are not directed at Mr. He, I have to bring them up to explain.

"For example, a few days ago someone raised the issue of mass language, didn't a friend who was impatient at heart come out in the talk of the Shen Bao at the same time, and immediately asked them to make a few mass language works to see?"

Is this sentence wrong again? Where is it wrong? It is impatient, it is to ask the writers who advocate mass language to first make a few standard mass language texts to see, indeed, I am wrong, I am too impatient, they advocate mass language; it is originally shouting slogans, praising each other, there is no need to look at the works, so the facts cannot be asked, and are not allowed to be asked, especially to ask them to make mass language standard texts and publish them to the public, it is really presumptuous, empty checks can be issued indiscriminately, but they are never allowed to be cashed, it is really a strange thing.

Mr. may be a writer, I will use magazines as an example to listen to Mr., for example, Mr. creates a magazine and publishes it in a bookstore, but the book buyer must first look at the contents of the book, the nature of the book, before buying it, I have never heard of it, the bookstore only has books to buy, but no books to read, to take a step back, my book has not yet been successful, first sell pre-sale coupons, it has a three-point slippery nature, but what is the content of this book, when will it be published, always report to people to listen to, so that everyone can go to buy, if only the name of the book, and the content is not allowed to be announced, the publication is also indefinite, it will make the general readers believe and buy, I think this method, only playing poker cards can only have a pair of small twos in hand, can make people a pair of "open" or "kan hu", throw more in the pile of cards, this is called sneaking, there is probably no such thing in the literary world.

Because my brain, is not as sensitive and authentic as Mr. Hua's, so I don't understand what kind of writing mass language is, so I want to ask the writers who advocate mass language to make a few standard mass language texts, so that the general stupid people - like my generation - can imitate, I know it is a big hit, offended Mr.'s taboo, not only refused to teach, but was ashamed and angry, mixed up, said that I am also a "impatient" friend, here I can't help but have some doubts, what kind of medicine are the gentlemen advocating mass language selling in the gourd ladle? I can't help but be "impatient."

Now take the vernacular movement in the May Fourth period as an example, the writers who advocated vernacular at that time, they themselves started to write vernacular to promote it. Regardless of whether their vernacular is a product of capitalism, they did not just talk vernacular, after all, they took out some things, what kind of things are the now advocating mass language taking out for us to see? The vernacular movement has been almost twenty years, may I ask whether the vernacular can be said to be completely successful, has the classical Chinese completely died? I dare not say this sentence; because the public documents are still full of classical Chinese, and most of the newspapers are classical Chinese, how can it be said that the vernacular is completely successful? Is the classical Chinese completely dead?

Since the vernacular is not completely successful yet, and then we promote mass language, this kind of "impatience" is probably fifty steps laughing at a hundred steps with my generation? I have no preparation for mass language, no plan, just shouting slogans, praising each other, is also "impatience", now that mass language has not come out, first do not allow people to speak, do not allow people to discuss, this kind of "impatience method" is probably more powerful than us, so I advise Mr., and slowly laugh at us "impatience", let's go ask others again, who is "impatient".

It's not just Mr. who laughs at my impatience, probably the gentlemen who advocate mass language, or want to laugh at my "impatience". They have several ways of laughing... One way of laughing is to say that when Mr. Sun Yat-sen advocated revolution, he never took out things to see first, and another way of laughing is to say that ideal is the mother of fact. The first statement is completely nonsense, there is absolutely no reason, because political revolution, or racial revolution, can use extraordinary means to exercise, and literature

Page 22

academic revolution, can never be done by extraordinary means. The second statement, although more reasonable, is actually somewhat inaccurate; recent people only see the foreigners' planes, cannons, wireless electricity, death rays, etc., are very powerful; but they have also gone through many scientists in the laboratory for a long time of research and experimentation, and then succeeded, not like Cao Cao asking Zuo Ci to eat, wanting to eat dragon liver, dragon liver arrives, wanting to eat four-gilled bass, four-gilled bass arrives, wanting to create mass language, I'm afraid it can't be as easy as Mr. Zuo Ci?

The writers who advocate mass language, naturally have a patriotic and people-loving psychology, not necessarily just put forward the three words mass language to deceive the public, deceive the illiterate. But we must also first conduct a thorough study of how the mass language is generated, and how to promote it to the public after it is generated, but since the three words mass language have been around, I have not seen a text designed for the mass language in a practical and dynamic way, but only wrote vernacular that was produced with capitalism and shouted the slogan of mass language.

The most ridiculous thing is that one gentleman wrote a few sentences of Pudong dialect and claimed it as Pudong mass language, and another gentleman wrote a few sentences of Shanghai dialect and happily claimed to be Shanghai mass language, these works came out, it is really a great bad luck in the literary world, I initially thought that it was deliberately done to oppose mass language, but later I found out that it was a loyal comrade of mass language, it is really the biggest joke in the world.

Some say that the three words mass language were produced because some people in the literary world, who want to climb up the ladder, worry that classical Chinese may be revived, so they simply create a mass language to resist, which is no different from a person who has a serious illness, the family does not go to a good doctor to diagnose and treat, but goes to a Taoist priest and witch to catch demons and subdue demons, the same stupidity. And a general group of shrimp soldiers and crab generals, then wheat straws are used as tokens of authority, they wave flags and shout, flying all over the stage, and those who wear silk scarves and feather fans, then sit high on the city head, raise their beards and nod and laugh, unfortunately I am not the kind who want to climb up the ladder, otherwise I would also promote a small mass language, so that a general group of shrimp soldiers and crab generals can also stir up a commotion and shout.

To unify thought and unify speech, only methods used by political power or political means can be used, the literary world is afraid of not having such power, such authority, now there are many people who doubt mass language, or oppose mass language, but people like Mr. Hua, do not use theory to convince, or use facts to explain, but use a mocking attitude to want to control everything, it is really boring, very pitiful; I advise Mr., do not wear a high hat, put on a red robe, mixed in the shrimp soldiers and crab generals team, shout and shout!

Mr. should be a specialist in literature, should have some of the writers of the attitude of research, humbly accommodate all aspects of opinions, is the right, do not put on the posture of the era of progressive, mass language expert's face, casually ridicule others, or indiscriminately scold others. Known as the literary world, not like the City God Temple in Shanghai, the Xuanmiao Temple in Suzhou, is a place dedicated to the sale of fists or the sale of hundred herbs pear paste sugar to deceive the audience.

What I advise you is very opposed to mass language, but it is not, because I said these words, but can arouse the reflection of the general advocate mass language gentlemen, desperately the mass language to study well, organize, if there is a mass language published and implemented one day, then my credit, not under the general shrimp soldiers and crab generals, if the mass language and even stillborn, can not produce, then the literary world should also clean up some of the air, do not get so smoky, I warn Mr. Hua, but laugh at me "impatient"! ｜End｜

War 266

— Cun Yin

The people of Verdun covered their ears and closed their eyes; their pounding hearts were caught in the panicked air.

|| War is a python!

They knew war was coming soon!

(The bugles of the army sounded, da, da, da! Black, gray, terror, and decline permeated the heavens, this ball-like sky! Already overflowing with the taste of blood!

The Lesde family’s home is far from the Maas River!

Maas River! It is the flow of our lives.

Yes, the people of the French Maas Riverbank all praise this blue and lively Maas River!

Young Lesde, his life is active, his nature is gentle, his skin is beautiful!

The army set off! He was inside too.

War broke out! He was inside too.

He left his hometown, parents, and beloved friend Molly; unexpectedly, he carried a rifle and a bundle on his body, and, and several rows of lethal bullets! He went far away! Stationed on the blue and lively banks of the Maas River.

His hometown is Durosey! Durosey! Durosey, where beautiful gales often rise! French Durosey!

He said...

|| War is terrible!

However, his words were a grain of sand in the desert!

So, he wandered silently! Vanished! Tearfully, heartbreakingly. Although, during the long European war, he was lucky not to die.

He returned to his hometown! Molly married the young pastor from the former church.

His father was captured by the enemy and has not returned.

His mother remarried someone else and does not recognize her own son!

One day.

He sat dejectedly in a cafe. He ran into Molly, who had once said to him, "Go forth! When you return, we will be even happier!" Next to her was a young man! That was the pastor!

Molly didn't recognize him!

Such a tattered person, full of beard! And scars, and wrinkles...

However, the outline of his face was still Lesde from five years ago!

|| Why are you so disgusting! Lesde wouldn't be like this.

He knew Molly was still thinking of him! || His heart ached. This was Molly's voice, absolutely true! Soon, he heard her say to that man...

|| If there is any news of Lesde, I will go find him! He is my dearest! You are... you really are...

| Stop!

Her words were soft!

Lesde felt very lucky! Because no one recognized him!

Molly and the others left! As they passed Lesde's seat, he stopped and stared!

|| Madam, what are you looking for?

He said this meaninglessly.

|| Are you Lesde?

She asked timidly.

|| Madam! I... I am not! You must be mistaken!

Her face flushed.

|| Molly! You ambitious woman! You still want to find that kind of fool? You, go find him in God's place!

Said the young man with the small mustache.

He knew he was the pastor! He had seen him come to the army to celebrate Mass!

They left.

He also went out with his head down.

People were noisy. Crowded. Gradually, it became deserted again! Ahead, all was desolate!

Lesde walked towards the wilderness without stopping.

Tears are turbid, his face is black, his wrinkles are deep, his beard is thick...

|| War is a sharp arrow piercing people's hearts!

They knew war was coming soon again!

The people of Verdun will hear this story from Durosey again!

A Ripe Dreamscape 268

— Sha Fei

On a sunny morning, I wander under the trees in the park, birds chirping above my head, already companions for three months; that unknown girl, haven't we met for ninety days?

From summer to autumn, we meet every day on the yellow sand path. We lower our heads to each other, or are we counting our own steps? It's so slight, like a lover's whisper.

My heart is melancholy.

The white geese by the pond, regardless of the flying yellow sand, chase each other. Sometimes they pounce on my heels, thinking someone is chasing me. Secretly peering around... An iron cage locking up a pair of deer... A few withered leaves flutter on the iron sand chair; the surface of the pond is disturbed like an restless heart; ninety days, this is a long-lasting memory | and ahead, a melancholy heart counting its own steps.

It's like a ripe dreamscape, that dreamscape lingers in my heart | Ah, one day, one day, that sunny morning will illuminate the illusion of this dreamscape.

Wait, count your own steps!

Three months, a long distance! The tail of the autumn wind will tear the last page of this set of calendars, will you ever see the joyous spring again, this ripe dreamscape?

Having walked to the end of the yellow sand path, look at the heaven and earth at that end! Pervaded by the great fog of London, where is the edge of your dreamscape?

My own steps disappear deep into the depths of a melancholy heart!

On a sunny morning, dragging my own slender shadow, from day ninety-one onwards.

Widow 269

— Wei Nan

Her precious youth was burned by the flames of famine, poverty, and unrequited love, losing her beautiful charm. She has no children, so she lives a lonely life without a husband. The crowd in this world is terribly indifferent, like snakes and scorpions, who would dare to approach them? In fact, they are more terrifying than tigers. They devour your youth, and when they are disgusted, they will throw you into the farthest reaches of the sky; countless women have suffered this kind of torture. She has never been abandoned by her husband, and has never been divorced like the "modern" people of today; he was loyal and conscientious, yet he did not live to old age with her, and suddenly left her alone in this desert-like human world to suffer!

She is my neighbor, only separated by a staircase, living her lonely and miserable life in the attic, the sadness of not having a husband, the loneliness of not having a son, she is suffering in this human world in a different way, living someone else's life. A sorrowful face, attacked by famine, relying only on her own hands to work for others, the money she earns is hardly enough to maintain her own life. That weak and pitiful woman, in this male-centered society, in the old living environment, how can a frail woman who is barely alive escape this danger of starvation in this treacherous crowd? Even if you can work, the sadness of the times is full of the misery of unemployment!

In this dirty world | especially in this evil and terrifying money-obsessed Shanghai, you pure and bright widow, you must be careful of the traps of mankind, in this vile, base, deceitful, and treacherous society, mankind will not have holy sympathy for you!

A Chronicle of Small Events of the Week 270

— Feng

The other day, a reporter from a certain news agency inquired with the International Trade Bureau and learned that the import value of shark fins, used by the upper and middle classes to entertain guests, was 8,980,072 gold units in the first seven months of this year, equivalent to 1,791,653 national currency units, which is a significant increase compared to the same period last year, and most of it is consumed in this port.

I truly envy the unshallow good fortune of the wealthy classes, but if the blood in your body is not completely cold, then look at the situation in the Northeast, the tense state in North China, and the overseas Chinese being driven back batch after batch by foreigners, how can they still eat such precious things?

Reuters Tokyo, August 30th. Minister of Education Matsuda has decided to ban the use of the terms "daddy" and "mommy" in elementary schools and kindergartens, stating that it damages Japanese customs.

Truly, Japan has now leaped to become an arrogant and domineering powerful nation, coming to learn the half-colonial Chinese children's terms "daddy" and "mommy." Only we Chinese, because of the poor national fortune, learn from foreigners in various ways, even the culture inherent in our country for thousands of years! Such as writing! Also unlucky and don't want it all together, what will such people think when they see it?

Reuters Berlin, August 30th. The government today ordered that all unmarried men and women under the age of twenty-five who hold public or private positions should be dismissed and replaced by older people, especially those with families.

Germany's advocacy of reproduction has been repeatedly emphasized; it is meticulous. This order naturally also advocates reproduction, but turning around to ask, what is the intention of advocating reproduction? This is very simple, nothing more than breeding them to sacrifice and become cannon fodder. Since our country's population is already so large, there is naturally no need to advocate reproduction again. We should advocate birth control, lest they become slaves, lest they be trampled by foreigners, lest they be given the cold shoulder by foreigners, lest they starve to death in batches.

Reuters London dispatch, August 30th. Chen Shangda, a Chinese military academy student, left his country in 1929 at the age of nineteen to visit his father's grave in Peru. Because he carried little funds, he often walked the journey, passing through Japan, North America, and South America, and arriving at his father's grave, having worn out fifty pairs of shoes and walked 15,000 miles.

Since the May Fourth Movement, non-filial piety has been practiced. Children treat their parents with the same attitude as they treat passersby, and they are still considered filial sons. Therefore, when parents are still alive, it is still like this. As for when the grave is already arched with trees, visiting is even more so. Only a few important people, returning home in glory, without a reason, just borrow the beautiful name of sweeping the grave to let people hear it. Chen Shangda is really a fool.

Amateur Mailbox

Notice 271

The original purpose of establishing this column was to mainly provide individual replies... or select and publish those with public discussion value. However, a small number of readers do not understand this purpose, regardless of the nature of the question, and request a public reply, and many do not include an address, so even the name is probably not real. This column cannot reply to such letters, no matter how important they are. It is found that the reason why readers are unwilling to tell their real name and location is probably because they fear that their secrets will be leaked, hindering their future. However, this column bears a strict responsibility for keeping the contents of all letters confidential. If you don’t mind announcing your real name, you can instruct to publish it under another name, so you don’t need to worry. It is hoped that readers will understand this point, and in the future, please write the detailed address clearly in your letter, otherwise we will not reply. Now, a portion of the names of the gentlemen who sent letters without addresses that have been received recently are extracted below to show a glimpse.

Chen Xizeng, Zheng Quansheng, Han Rongjiu, Zhang Shili, Hu Shijing, Wu Lianfang, Lin Jing, Yu Li, Xing Zhong, He Guiying, Zhao Zusi, Liu Rihong, Wu Qiying, Chen Mengjue, Jin Yi, Liu Shanshi, Xu Zhongde, Hun He, Zi Jing, Peng Feng, Shuying, Cao Zhixin, Wang Zhiliang, Tian Fang, Hong Ziping, Jiang Chen Baiying, Yi Shengben, Ye Xiuying, Yilan, Song Mao Nv, Mo Fahua, Hai Ning Ren, Zhou Yaozong, Yu Ziming, Zheng Yaying, Dong Yi Dan, Yang Jidu, Shao Wenzhong, Zhang Lianshu, Jian Biao, Guangming, Zhu Bowei, etc.

Also, the editor of this mailbox has been ill for a long time, resulting in a large number of letters being put on hold. Now that he has recovered, he will decide to reply separately as soon as possible within the next few days, and ask readers to understand.

Novel

The Ball (4) 272

— Translated by Hungarian M. Zhou Kai Zu Shiheng

Regarding this point, she scolded me even more, scolding me for being a little goose and telling me that soon I would understand my absurdity; after saying these threatening words, she left me. I was busy preparing for the dance, and I was so busy until the evening that everything was ready. According to the officer's suggestion, I tied a wide red, white, and green ribbon around my waist, and on my head, I only tied a rose flower of red and white, paired with green leaves, and it became a national beauty. I had never discovered how good these colors mixed together were before.

The two officers waited with great joy, saying so many polite things to us, I couldn't imagine how they learned them. I had to cover up my embarrassment with a smile.

"Oh, you see, this matter will end in tears," my mother said, but she continued to tidy up my clothes, changing this one, changing that one, as if if they took me away, at least it would make them feel that everything was in order.

The two officers accompanied us to the ballroom. I had already happily thought about the impact that my national-colored ribbon and our two handsome young men would have on the gathering, and as we walked in, I was still thinking that if everyone in the room had square heads, we could have the only two round-headed people.

But my error and surprise were extreme. Almost every one of my female companions had at least two national-colored ribbons like me, and as for the officers, our two warriors could only be considered third-rate figures among them. Each one was more cordial, charming, beautiful, and lively - how could such people shed so much blood!

One of them especially caught my attention, not just me, everyone did. He was a young captain! His movingly beautiful face and tall, elegant posture were extremely suitable for the trimmed military uniform, which seemed to be molded on his body. Next, there was his dancing! How energetically he danced the mazurka and the czardas! Someone would rush through the crowd and embrace him! This is not me saying myself. Moreover, more endearing than his dancing and his solicitousness was the purity in his dazed black eyes. In less than an hour, every daughter in this room had fallen in love with him. I am not excluding myself. If they are so reckless on the battlefield, I don't know what anyone can resist them. But suddenly he stepped in front of me and asked me to dance the next quadrille with him, imagine my emotions at this time!
